<span id="freeTextContainer2453409757068927836">Nine years after leaving in disgrace, Olivia Morrison is coming home again with her eight-year-old, Sara, to put things right with the Archer clan. But there is no welcome for the prodigal daughter at the lavish Louisiana estate.<br /><br />Her stepcousin, Seth, once her only comfort, is icy, dangerously attractive — and engaged. Her formidable stepgrandfather collapses with a heart a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2453409757068927836">Nine years after leaving in disgrace, Olivia Morrison is coming home again with her eight-year-old, Sara, to put things right with the Archer clan. But there is no welcome for the prodigal daughter at the lavish Louisiana estate.<br /><br />Her stepcousin, Seth, once her only comfort, is icy, dangerously attractive — and engaged. Her formidable stepgrandfather collapses with a heart attack at the sight of her, gasping her dead mother’s name: “Selena!”<br /><br />The bayou echoes with memories of her mother’s mysterious death. Suicide by drowning, they said. But Olivia’s terrifying nightmares suggest another story. She is determined to learn the truth, and to face a newly ignited passion for Seth, who is too close for comfort, despite his vows. <br /><br />When a new danger threatens her and her daughter, Olivia must find the courage to confront her old demons ... and uncover a shocking secret buried in the long-forgotten past....</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10957673764048766467">This is a reread, although I don't remember the plot exactly. Must have read it BG (before Goodreads). Which is great for a reread. All the character and the places seem familiar but I have no idea who the baddie is. This book is everything a great romantic-suspense should be. It has great tension between the H/h, a plot that keeps you guessing until the very end and really hot sex scenes.<br /><br />Olivia has returned to the LaAngelle plantation she left at 18 in a snit against Seth, a step-cousin, and Bi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10957673764048766467">This is a reread, although I don't remember the plot exactly. Must have read it BG (before Goodreads). Which is great for a reread. All the character and the places seem familiar but I have no idea who the baddie is. This book is everything a great romantic-suspense should be. It has great tension between the H/h, a plot that keeps you guessing until the very end and really hot sex scenes.<br /><br />Olivia has returned to the LaAngelle plantation she left at 18 in a snit against Seth, a step-cousin, and Big John her step-grandfather, who at 87 has a heart attack at seeing her again. Olivia and her 8 year old daughter, Sara, have been invited to return by Seth's mother, Callie, who is facing cancer treatment and has decided that Olivia and the Archer family need to kiss and make-up. Seth and Olivia have a real love-hate thing going that is really intriguing as he is now engaged.<br /><br />There is a real nasty who had been killing young girls for 30 years. Who he is and how he is related is something that the layers of this plot will revel in due time. One thing I know, Seth and Olivia have some very hot, intense unfinished business to attend to.</span>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8956777-lafleurbleue?shelf=romantic-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">romantic-suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer512743829">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5387026511242933592">It felt really long and frankly a bit boring. Neither the suspense, nor the romance are great. Let's start with the suspense: poor Olivia had horrible vivid dreams ever since she came back in her childhood's house, her daughter also went through similar bad dreams. However once again she procrastinated and did nothing about those until very very late. There are a few discrepancies in the story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ like when the bad guy managed to get both into her room and her daughter's room, even i</span></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5387026511242933592">It felt really long and frankly a bit boring. Neither the suspense, nor the romance are great. Let's start with the suspense: poor Olivia had horrible vivid dreams ever since she came back in her childhood's house, her daughter also went through similar bad dreams. However once again she procrastinated and did nothing about those until very very late. There are a few discrepancies in the story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ like when the bad guy managed to get both into her room and her daughter's room, even if she changed the lock on the French windows that he used to come through every time before  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Sara, her daughter, is so perfect, despite being plump, that she did not seem real, more like a doll. <br />Moving to the romance, I absolutely hated that the main couple grew up together from early infancy on as cousins, even if only step-cousins with no shared blood. Add to that she also briefly almost considered dating another cousin and that was too much. <br />The high rating received by this book puzzles me, even though I have no complaint regarding the writing. One of the supposedly highly emotional moment in the book left me totally cold.<br />A miss.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1250572516">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250572516" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/667272-christine" class="left imgcol" title="Christine"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1376230788p2/667272.jpg" alt="Christine" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1250572516?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/667272-christine" class="user" title="Christine">Christine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/667272-christine?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/667272-christine?shelf=suspense-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/667272-christine?shelf=paranormal" class="actionLinkLite">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1250572516">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13597126539466837904">I'm probably being too hard on this book, given that it was an engaging, easy read. There was a lot of family drama that was particularly well done, and I enjoyed the romance.<br /><br />HOWEVER ...<br /><br />This novel opens with a mother going in to help her daughter, who just wet the bed again. The next morning, the mother finds her daughter dead in her bed and the whole incident was blamed on the husband, with reports saying he killed his daughter for wetting the bed. <br /><br />The husband didn't do it. This was clear from</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13597126539466837904">I'm probably being too hard on this book, given that it was an engaging, easy read. There was a lot of family drama that was particularly well done, and I enjoyed the romance.<br /><br />HOWEVER ...<br /><br />This novel opens with a mother going in to help her daughter, who just wet the bed again. The next morning, the mother finds her daughter dead in her bed and the whole incident was blamed on the husband, with reports saying he killed his daughter for wetting the bed. <br /><br />The husband didn't do it. This was clear from the beginning. But though the reader eventually learned the identity of the killer, the initial incident was left unresolved because there was no way to link that case to the killer. As far as I can tell, the girl's father is still in prison for a crime he didn't commit and will be until he dies. <br /><br />This is a huge structural problem. You don't begin with a hugely horrific scene that you fail to fully resolve by the end of the book. That's why I can't give this book an honest three stars. <br /><br />I would also add two other things:<br /><br />1. The suspense was poorly woven into the main action of the story. The main characters mostly lived their lives, with occasional, unconnected scenes from the killer's POV to let us know he was still out there. Karen Robards has used this strategy before, and it has never worked for me. <br /><br />2. The killer's identity was obvious.<br /><br />3. The ghostly element was pretty weak. (But this is likely a personal opinion. I have set ideas about how paranormal elements should be woven into stories, and it is never as a convenient way to resolve things at the climax.)<br /><br />Overall, I don't recommend this one. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13597126539466837904">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103512713" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5259162-darlene" class="left imgcol" title="Darlene"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1363357921p2/5259162.jpg" alt="Darlene" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1103512713?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 12, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5259162-darlene" class="user" title="Darlene">Darlene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1103512713">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8581323704985102105">When first started reading chapter 1, then chapter 2, I admit was a little confused. Chapter 1 was an earlier story line that would intertwine with the rest of the story line. I liked how the chapters were short. I hate reading a book with super long chapters because they tend to make you feel like you are lost by time you come to the end of them. This book is about family, love lost and found again. While reading, and wondering who it was that was able to sneak into houses without being detecte</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8581323704985102105">When first started reading chapter 1, then chapter 2, I admit was a little confused. Chapter 1 was an earlier story line that would intertwine with the rest of the story line. I liked how the chapters were short. I hate reading a book with super long chapters because they tend to make you feel like you are lost by time you come to the end of them. This book is about family, love lost and found again. While reading, and wondering who it was that was able to sneak into houses without being detected and taking little girls, I was running through a list of suspects. The span was like a 30 year period. When I found out it was the uncle, I knew my hunches were right when I started to suspect a family member. In the end, he took his own life instead of Olivia's or Sara's. He knew that he was caught and would be put in jail probably for life. Would have liked to know his reason for it. Why he liked to do what he had done. The dreams that Olivia kept having, after awhile, I figured out that she must have witnessed her mothers drowning and perhaps eventually may have remembered even more, the reason for the uncle to take her too, again, so she wouldn't tell. Didn't expect him to drug Big John so he wouldn't tell anything he may have known. Was glad that in the end, Olivia, Seth, Sara and Chloe were all going to be a family. Only in the south is it normal for family to become family!! Of course, being step cousins, they are family, but then when they marry, the will be a family. This was a good book and I look forward to reading more by Ms Robards. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8581323704985102105">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5105168687154094006">I chose this book from a GoodReads list of recommendations. Well, I think I was a bit too trusting. I was expecting a mystery/ghost story; what I got was a Harlequin romance complete with the overdone descriptions (down to the color of nylons worn by the protagonist) and gratuitous textual porn scenes. I won't be reading any more Karen Robards books in the future, and if I'm looking for real romance, I'll go to Nicholas Sparks.<br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer708296748'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer708296748">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11635839630122095977">Olivia is returning home to LaAngelle after 9 years away...with her 8 year old daughter Sara. But it's harder to just resume her place in the family now - not only has she grown up, but she's a virtual stranger. And her stepcousin Seth doesn't seem inclined to forgive her right away. As Olivia struggles to make amends, take care of her daughter (especially given her vulnerable nature) and deal with two family illnesses, she also faces a growing attraction for Seth (who is engaged to be married).</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11635839630122095977">Olivia is returning home to LaAngelle after 9 years away...with her 8 year old daughter Sara. But it's harder to just resume her place in the family now - not only has she grown up, but she's a virtual stranger. And her stepcousin Seth doesn't seem inclined to forgive her right away. As Olivia struggles to make amends, take care of her daughter (especially given her vulnerable nature) and deal with two family illnesses, she also faces a growing attraction for Seth (who is engaged to be married). Under all of this is ever increasing nightmares about her own mother's death. And now Sara is having nightmares as well. <br /><br />I actually liked this book quite a bit. I wasn't weirded out by the whole stepcousins thing. They weren't blood related and I although Seth had previously felt a brotherly affection for her, he admits that it had morphed into a not-so-familial, lustful feeling. Both of them recognize that this is different from the norm, but there are not familial feelings mixed in...no one minute thinking of the other as brotherly and the next lusting after them (I remember reading a book with that - eew). I liked both of the characters. Olivia came back ready to face her mistakes and try to make things better. I think she showed a whole lot more restraint in not stepping into parent Chloe in the face of her father's relative neglect - so I admit to some admiration. Seth was very hot and perfectly alpha and clueless about children. <br /><br />The murder mystery was pretty good - but I'd kind of already figured out what happened before the end. It was still exciting, but it was predictable. I admit, I had no idea what the killer was actually doing with his victims though, until the end. Yikes. There was a corny moment or two (especially Seth teaching a Brownie troop about bullying). </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11635839630122095977">...more</a>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4653461-lita-bouquard?shelf=mystery-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-suspense</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer785761936">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16708283584698614710">If you've never read Karen Robards please don't start with this book. It is not her best. Robards excels at the suspense/mystery/romance dramas and used to occasionally have funny scenes interwoven. Ghost Moon was a creepy, pedophilic? story of a reformed wild young woman who is now a single parent and returning to her roots. Olivia goes back to her step family for a visit at the invite of an ailing aunt. Her sweet, chubby daughter enjoys the bayou country and they spend precious time together a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16708283584698614710">If you've never read Karen Robards please don't start with this book. It is not her best. Robards excels at the suspense/mystery/romance dramas and used to occasionally have funny scenes interwoven. Ghost Moon was a creepy, pedophilic? story of a reformed wild young woman who is now a single parent and returning to her roots. Olivia goes back to her step family for a visit at the invite of an ailing aunt. Her sweet, chubby daughter enjoys the bayou country and they spend precious time together and adjusting to family/friends and past history. Olivia helps with her cousin Seth's spoiled angry daughter who acts out, especially against Seth's fiance. Olivia begins having nightmares and so does her daughter. She begins to question why she has so few memories of her deceased mother and dreams of her often. When offered the opportunity to stay, they do, but Olivia begins to feel attracted to her "cousin" Seth. The villian was easy to predict, but I have to admit after the first story of a child's abduction I skipped those chapters. They were just not what I wanted to read about. This book had a lot of death, dying, and was a dark one for Robards. If you want to try her books read some very early books like One Summer. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/3260903-stephanie-once-upon-a-chapter" class="user" title="Stephanie (Once Upon a Chapter)">Stephanie (Once Upon a Chapter)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3260903-stephanie-once-upon-a-chapter?shelf=read-in-2010" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer118076517'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer118076517">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6337013304933356298"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://onceuponachapter.com/2010/08/ghost-moon-by-karen-robards.html">This review was originally posted on Once Upon a Chapter</a><a rel="nofollow" href="http://onceuponachapter.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/banner-review1.png"> <img width="300" height="127" class="escapedImg" alt="banner-review(1)" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404887136i/10292568.png" /></a><br /><br /><br /><br />Olivia Morrison has been summoned home by her dear Aunt Callie. Aunt Callie is ill and Olivia's grandfather, Big John, is getting on in years. Olivia decides nine years away from the one place she knew as home is long enough. She and her daughter Sara go home to the LaAngelle Plantation she called home as a child. The last night she was in the house she and her stepcousin Seth had gotten into a heated battle. Afterwards, Olivia eloped and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6337013304933356298"><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://onceuponachapter.com/2010/08/ghost-moon-by-karen-robards.html">This review was originally posted on Once Upon a Chapter</a><a rel="nofollow" href="http://onceuponachapter.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/07/banner-review1.png">
  <img width="300" height="127" class="escapedImg" alt="banner-review(1)" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404887136i/10292568.png" /></a><br /><br /><br /><br />Olivia Morrison has been summoned home by her dear Aunt Callie. Aunt Callie is ill and Olivia's grandfather, Big John, is getting on in years. Olivia decides nine years away from the one place she knew as home is long enough. She and her daughter Sara go home to the LaAngelle Plantation she called home as a child. The last night she was in the house she and her stepcousin Seth had gotten into a heated battle. Afterwards, Olivia eloped and hadn't been back since.<br /><br />Olivia doesn't get the welcome home reception she had expected. In fact her grandfather looks at her and has a heart attack on the spot. If it weren't for Aunt Callie Olivia would have gone back home. She realizes how far she has actually distanced herself and her daughter from her large extended family. Olivia makes an effort to get to know her family again. Shortly after she returns, Olivia starts to have nightmares of her mother's suicide and always from the perception of an onlooker by the lake. Voices tell her to run from the lake, to run and run far away.<br /><br />Between the nightmares and her budding attraction to the man she always perceived as a cousin, Olivia has a lot on her plate. She acknowledges that she can't have feelings for Seth. After all, he's getting married to another woman in six weeks. Her nightmares bring her heart stopping fear at night and leave her wondering if her mother's suicide was even a suicide at all.<br /><br />Oh my! For much of the book, there seem to be three major plot points going on. One takes place in the past and then there seem to be two in the present. Robards can write a stunning plot and I was glued to the book the whole time with a perplexed look on my face. The romance was a little off. It seemed like it took half of the book to find out that they were attracted to each other, another quarter of the book fighting that attraction and then the last quarter was split between the recognition of their love and the ending of the suspense plot.<br /><br />This book was awesome as far as the suspense plot was concerned. At the end of the book, I was floored. I had a hunch of who the villain would be as far as relation to our heroine, Olivia. I was shocked and pleasantly surprised that the last person I suspected was the bad guy. Believe me, up until the last chapter or two I had several choices to pick from. The ending was deliciously spine tingling. If you like romantic suspense and don't mind a heavy focus on the suspense and a lesser focus on the romance, you should make it a point to pick this book up.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6337013304933356298">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13829772864175209448">Finally! This is the best book I've read in a long time. It makes me want to go out and buy every Karen Robards novel I can find. <br />Olivia, an orphan, was raised by her step family on LaAngelle Plantation in Louisiana. Once she reached her teens, she ran wild. Her cousin Seth tried to keep her in line, but they just butted heads. Olivia eloped with a rodeo star. She had a daughter, then the marriage failed. Olivia was too proud to go back home. Now, her Aunt Callie has sent a personal invitation t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13829772864175209448">Finally! This is the best book I've read in a long time. It makes me want to go out and buy every Karen Robards novel I can find. <br />Olivia, an orphan, was raised by her step family on LaAngelle Plantation in Louisiana. Once she reached her teens, she ran wild. Her cousin Seth tried to keep her in line, but they just butted heads. Olivia eloped with a rodeo star. She had a daughter, then the marriage failed. Olivia was too proud to go back home. Now, her Aunt Callie has sent a personal invitation to her, asking Olivia to visit. <br />Once she arrives, all hell breaks loose. <br />Olivia is haunted by her mother's death. She starts having nightmares about it. She is also dealing with Seth, who is still angry with her. Aunt Callie is ill with cancer, her step grandfather, Big John, has a heart attack at the sight of her, and Seth's daughter is a brat. <br />Robard's descriptions of the area are lush and beautiful. The characters are believable and human. We know something terrible has been going on for a long time and Olivia and Sara are in danger. Meanwhile, Seth learns a few parenting lessons from Olivia, and they are both stunned by their attraction to each other. This opens Seth's eyes and he begins to question his upcoming marriage. The friendship between Seth and Olivia develops as well as their physical attraction. Tragedy strikes, bringing them together, mind ans body. But, Olivia still can't shake her nightmares. Tension slowly builds until it is nearly unbearable. The crimes are the worst you can imagine and are not for the faint of heart.<br />This gets an A.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_449906072">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449906072" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11676864-raynell" class="left imgcol" title="Raynell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1349610247p2/11676864.jpg" alt="Raynell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/449906072?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11676864-raynell" class="user" title="Raynell">Raynell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer449906072">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17072939779563519312">Usually, I like some romance in my thrillers, but in this case, I'd rather not have it at all. Before I list my reasons why, I'll get the plotting, prose and pacing out of the way.<br /><br />Ms. Robards writes very well, and although she has a tendency to go slow midway, it's tolerable enough. The mystery of a paedophile/serial killer is woven OK -- not skillfully though as not enough details are offered/revealed to resolve the huge convenience factors peppered within the story. But it would have been suff</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17072939779563519312">Usually, I like some romance in my thrillers, but in this case, I'd rather not have it at all. Before I list my reasons why, I'll get the plotting, prose and pacing out of the way.<br /><br />Ms. Robards writes very well, and although she has a tendency to go slow midway, it's tolerable enough. The mystery of a paedophile/serial killer is woven OK -- not skillfully though as not enough details are offered/revealed to resolve the huge convenience factors peppered within the story. But it would have been sufficient to increase the rating to at most an A- or 4.5 stars.<br /><br />What cost the book the rating is Olivia and to a lesser degree Seth and their cheating. I don't believe in couples staying together if one party is in love or attracted to another; in that respect, I think the relationship should be dissolved. I can even forgive a sexual slip-up -- the whole swept-away-by-passion and we-didn't-mean-it-to-happen cliches. What alienated me from the two mains was the fact that there was NO GUILT over the cheating AT ALL.<br /><br />Since the book is mainly from Olivia's POV, my dislike is for her mostly. After the sex happened, I expected her to feel some guilt, especially when she remembers that Seth is engaged and encounters the fiancée. You know, like any normal decent but flawed human. But instead, I was treated to pages of how jealous Olivia was to see Mallory, the fiancée, kissing or touching Seth, etc. Even when Olivia participates in discussions over the wedding preparations with Mallory, the only negative thoughts Olivia have are of jealousy. Not "Oh dear, I slept with your man and here you are blithely planning your wedding and thinking everything is OK with your relationship, I'm such a slut and your man is a wishy-washy man-whore, but I love him, and I'm so sorry." Anyway, this only serves to present Olivia as very self-centered and selfish, and immensely unlikeable, and by the time the final showdown occurred with the villain (totally called it, by the way, and almost from the moment the character was introduced, I might add), I was actually rooting for the murderer to succeed in killing Olivia before he gets caught.<br /><br />Final Grade: a disappointing C.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17072939779563519312">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9013597120480725305">This book actually went differently than any other Karen Robards book I have read. The danger really wasn't all that obvious until the very ending. It kept going along as just a story where a woman moves back to the town where she grew up and found a romance with someone from her past.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9013597120480725305">This book actually went differently than any other Karen Robards book I have read. The danger really wasn't all that obvious until the very ending. It kept going along as just a story where a woman moves back to the town where she grew up and found a romance with someone from her past. The fact that it was her Uncle Charlie was the big surprise, but it was a surprise to find out what he was really doing.. It was also kind of sick, and it was a good thing he was stopped before he hurt Sara or Olivia. I wish the story had went a bit further, like what happened to the bodies of the girls he had taken, whether the family members were located, and which ones, and whether the first girl, Missy, whether her father was cleared, though it didn't come out that he had killed her, so it probably wouldn't have ever been known. The thing I loved about this book, is that it had a really big surprise ending. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText138483579063028576">** contains spoilers ** I liked how this story leapt from the 1970s to present time. It had me guessing who was who in the story (who the little girls were and who the killer was -- at one point, I was convinced the killer was Lamar, or his dad since Lamar would have been too young). <br /><br />The storyline was okay. It seems weird to me that cousins would fall in love. I get that they're stepcousins, but still, the fact that they always thought of each other as brother and sister growing up made them too close to end up together. <br /><br />The one thing that drove me nuts though was all the descriptions of what people were wearing. Who cares, really? Unless it matters to the story like what Chloe wore to her nana's funeral, I really don't care. I found myself skimming through a lot of the descriptive passages.<br /><br />My favorite part was the conversation between Callie &amp; Chloe the night she died.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16509096353691036163">I went from locking windows, to being too afraid to look under my bed, to fanning from the "heat of desire and passion" to wipeing tears from my eyes with an aching heart. An emotional ride. Such VIVID almost poetic descriptions to the landscapes/areas that I could almost taste the thick , humid air of Louisiana and could hear the irritating buzz of the mosquitos. The unfolding mystery was very well done. The "bad guy" was logical in the end, but not so obvious to make it too easy for us to figure out too early in the book. The end of the story was wrapped up cohesively over a good span instead of everything coming to an abrupt end within 2 pages. Those disappoint me. Don't like that. <br />The only reason I didn't give this book a 5 star is because I really don't like to read about child murders. Other than that, this was a very good mystery. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11980594058517587215">Only my borderline OCD personality kept me from tossing this one aside. Unfortunately I feel compelled to finish any book I start, otherwise this one never would have made it to the "has been read" bookshelf. <br /><br />I would classify Ghost Moon as romantic suspense. Not my usual genre but it caught my eye while at a used bookstore. Instead of wracking my brain trying to find redeeming qualities and offer a lengthy synopsis I'll keep it short and sweet. This one was a bore. It easily could have been 100 pages shorter and still got the job done. It plodded on and on, moving mind-boggingly slow, to the oh-so-neatly resolved ending. <br /><br />I think it's safe to say that after this less than successful foray into the work of Karen Robards...   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8546924587373698836">Cliches abound in this gothic romance novel. Hysterical amnesia to propel the plot, really? The romance never really gets off the ground due to far too many secondary characters and a deeply disturbing subplot about a serial killer preying on little girls. The hero is engaged at the start of the novel but soon ditches his fiancee with the career for Olivia who is the ideal mother. He could have hired a nanny and gone through with the wedding but then he'd miss the fun of ditching his fiance while she's clutching their wedding invitations. The penultimate scene is deeply traumatic, leaving this reader thinking all the characters will need years of therapy. But all that traumatization is magically fixed with a proposal. Ugh.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_164693743">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/164693743" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/949924-maria" class="left imgcol" title="Maria"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1242245373p2/949924.jpg" alt="Maria" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/164693743?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 01, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/949924-maria" class="user" title="Maria">Maria</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/949924-maria?shelf=romantic-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">romantic-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer164693743">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer290772630053527820">Due to the subject matter, this book is difficult to read, at least for any mother, but Ms. Robards has such a way with suspense that you force yourself to deal with the horror even as you race-read to make sure Olivia and Sara end up okay. I usually can guess who-done-it much more quickly than I did this time. I was almost at the end before I figured it out. As if that is not enough, the romance part is very well done, drawn out smoothly and slowly to its conclusion. If you like your relationsh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText290772630053527820">Due to the subject matter, this book is difficult to read, at least for any mother, but Ms. Robards has such a way with suspense that you force yourself to deal with the horror even as you race-read to make sure Olivia and Sara end up okay. I usually can guess who-done-it much more quickly than I did this time. I was almost at the end before I figured it out. As if that is not enough, the romance part is very well done, drawn out smoothly and slowly to its conclusion. If you like your relationships to develop quickly with a too-fast-off-the-mark jump start, this book is not for you. You get the feeling that this relationship takes its time to come about and will last a life time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="290772630053527820">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('H+TORXspNNbSmGD4ztJCCAMfe5PLpYLjxhdV8ugpNCZ6MPGWifsgLF5AFEOws6S6Sui4ioJ4xUmsHlBgJLzCYw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+xHqwUjQrQqA6EYrquRmIEeMGhypYd1LD1XgjgUzB4eexdUSugK58AwwMpDUhYCSDnvZBeC8muFlXOUcyabxwg==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/33408.Karen_Robards">About Karen Robards</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/33408.Karen_Robards"><img alt="33408" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1215007627p2/33408.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer3498308156122346855">Karen was born on 24 August 1954 in Louisville, Kentucky, USA. She has been writing since she was a teenager. She sold her first short story, when was very young, and was published in the December 1973 Reader's Digest, but she cannot sold her first romance novel until 1981, when she was 24. After it, she dropped out of law school to pursue her writing career. Today, a regular on the New York Times</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3498308156122346855">Karen was born on 24 August 1954 in Louisville, Kentucky, USA. She has been writing since she was a teenager. She sold her first short story, when was very young, and was published in the December 1973 Reader's Digest, but she cannot sold her first romance novel until 1981, when she was 24. After it, she dropped out of law school to pursue her writing career. Today, a regular on the New York Times, USA Today and Publishers Weekly bestseller lists, among others, she is the winner of six Affaire de Coeur Silver Pen Awards for favorite romance author, as well as numerous other awards. She writes historical and contemporary romances. Her work has been translated into eleven languages, and has won awards from both Romantic Times and Affaire de Coeur.<br /><br />Karen lives in native Louisville with her husband, Doug Robards, and their three sons Peter (b. 1983), Christopher "Chris" (b. 1989), and Jack (b. 1994). She says: "I read, I write, and I chauffeur children," she says with a laugh. "That's my life."<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3498308156122346855">...more</a>
